<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Structures">Structures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bremen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Structures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bremen_fallturm2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Bremen_fallturm2.jpg/170px-Bremen_fallturm2.jpg" width="170" height="385" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Bremen_fallturm2.jpg/255px-Bremen_fallturm2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/98/Bremen_fallturm2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="265" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bremen_fallturm2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i><a href="/wiki/Fallturm_Bremen" title="Fallturm Bremen">Fallturm</a></i> (Drop Tower) of the University of Bremen</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mediumwave_transmitter_Bremen" title="Mediumwave transmitter Bremen">Mediumwave transmitter Bremen</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fallturm_Bremen" title="Fallturm Bremen">Fallturm Bremen</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bremen_TV_tower" title="Bremen TV tower">Bremen-Walle Telecommunication Tower</a></li>
</ul>
<p>The <i>Freie Waldorfschule</i> in Bremen-Sebaldsbrück was Germany's first school built to the <i><a href="/wiki/Passive_house" title="Passive house">Passivhaus</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Low-energy_house" title="Low-energy house">low-energy building</a> standard.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bremen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to data from the Organization of Economic Cooperation and Development, Bremen had a GDP per capita of $53,379 in 2013, higher than the average for Germany as a whole. For comparison, in 2013, the World Bank reported Germany had a GDP per capita of $46,268, and the EU overall had a GDP per capita of $35,408 in the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bremen is the second development centre of the region, after <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>. It forms part of the production network of <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> SAS and this is where equipping of the wing units for all widebody Airbus aircraft and the manufacture of small sheet metal parts takes place. Structural assembly, including that of metal landing flaps, is another focal point. Within the framework of <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> production, assembly of the landing flaps (high lift systems) is carried out here. The pre-final assembly of the fuselage section (excluding the cockpit) of the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A400M" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A400M">A400M</a> military transport aircraft takes place before delivery on to Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>More than 3,100 persons are employed at Bremen, the second largest Airbus site in Germany. As part of the Centre of Excellence – Wing/Pylon, Bremen is responsible for the design and manufacture of high-lift systems for the wings of Airbus aircraft. The entire process chain for the high-lift elements is established here, including the project office, technology engineering, flight physics, system engineering, structure development, verification tests, structural assembly, wing equipping and ultimate delivery to the final assembly line. In addition, Bremen manufactures sheet metal parts like clips and thrust crests for all Airbus aircraft as part of the Centre of Excellence – Fuselage and Cabin.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Bremen there is a plant of <a href="/wiki/EADS_Astrium" class="mw-redirect" title="EADS Astrium">EADS Astrium</a> and the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/OHB-System" class="mw-redirect" title="OHB-System">OHB-System</a>, respectively the first and the third space companies of European Union.</p>
<p>There is also a <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a> factory in Bremen, building the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_C-Class" title="Mercedes-Benz C-Class">C</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_CLK-Class" title="Mercedes-Benz CLK-Class">CLK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_SL-Class" title="Mercedes-Benz SL-Class">SL</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_SLK-Class" title="Mercedes-Benz SLK-Class">SLK</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_GLK-Class" title="Mercedes-Benz GLK-Class">GLK</a> series of cars.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Beck%27s_Brewery" title="Beck's Brewery">Beck &amp; Co</a>'s headlining brew Beck's and <a href="/wiki/St._Pauli_Girl" title="St. Pauli Girl">St Pauli Girl</a> beers are brewed in Bremen. In past centuries when Bremen's port was the "key to Europe", the city also had a large number of wine importers, but the number is down to a precious few. Apart from that there is another link between Bremen and wine: about 800 years ago, quality wines were produced here. The largest <a href="/wiki/Wine_cellar" title="Wine cellar">wine cellar</a> in the world is located in Bremen (below the city's main square), which was once said to hold over 1 million bottles, but during WWII was raided by occupying forces.</p>
<p>A large number of food producing or trading companies are located in Bremen with their German or European headquarters: <a href="/wiki/Anheuser-Busch" title="Anheuser-Busch">Anheuser-Busch</a> InBev (Beck's Brewery), <a href="/wiki/Kellogg_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Kellogg Company">Kellogg's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kraft_Foods" title="Kraft Foods">Kraft Foods</a> (Kraft, Jacobs Coffee, Milka Chocolate, Milram, Miràcoli), Frosta (frosted food), Nordsee (chain of sea fast food), <a href="/wiki/Melitta" title="Melitta">Melitta</a> Kaffee, Eduscho Kaffee, Azul Kaffee, Vitakraft (pet food for birds and fishes), Atlanta AG (Chiquita banana), chocolatier <a href="/wiki/Hachez" title="Hachez">Hachez</a> (fine chocolate and confiserie), feodora chocolatier.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bremer_Woll-K%C3%A4mmerei" title="Bremer Woll-Kämmerei">Bremer Woll-Kämmerei</a> (BWK), a worldwide operating company for manufacturing wool and trading in wool and similar products, is headquartered in Bremen.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bremen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bremen_Hbf_pano.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Bremen_Hbf_pano.jpg/220px-Bremen_Hbf_pano.jpg" width="220" height="80" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Bremen_Hbf_pano.jpg/330px-Bremen_Hbf_pano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Bremen_Hbf_pano.jpg/440px-Bremen_Hbf_pano.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7937" data-file-height="2871" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bremen_Hbf_pano.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bremen_Central_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Bremen Central Station">Bremen Central Station</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sbahnbremen102010.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Sbahnbremen102010.svg/300px-Sbahnbremen102010.svg.png" width="300" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Sbahnbremen102010.svg/450px-Sbahnbremen102010.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Sbahnbremen102010.svg/600px-Sbahnbremen102010.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="820" data-file-height="820" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sbahnbremen102010.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the Bremen S-Bahn</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bremen has an <a href="/wiki/Bremen_Airport" title="Bremen Airport">international airport</a> situated 3&#160;km (2&#160;mi) south of the city centre.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Bremen" title="Trams in Bremen">Trams in Bremen</a> and local <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">bus</a> services are offered by the <a href="/wiki/Bremer_Stra%C3%9Fenbahn_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Bremer Straßenbahn AG">Bremer Straßenbahn AG</a> (translates from German as <i>Bremen Tramways Corporation</i>), often abbreviated BSAG, the <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">public transport</a> provider for Bremen.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bremen_S-Bahn" title="Bremen S-Bahn">Bremen S-Bahn</a> covers the <a href="/wiki/Bremen/Oldenburg_Metropolitan_Region" title="Bremen/Oldenburg Metropolitan Region">Bremen/Oldenburg Metropolitan Region</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Bremerhaven" title="Bremerhaven">Bremerhaven</a> in the north to <a href="/wiki/Twistringen" title="Twistringen">Twistringen</a> in the south and from <a href="/wiki/Oldenburg" title="Oldenburg">Oldenburg</a> in the west, centred on <a href="/wiki/Bremen_Central_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Bremen Central Station">Bremen Central Station</a>. It has been in operation since 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> This network unified existing regional transport in Bremen as well as surrounding cities, including <a href="/wiki/Bremerhaven" title="Bremerhaven">Bremerhaven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delmenhorst" title="Delmenhorst">Delmenhorst</a>, <a href="/wiki/Twistringen" title="Twistringen">Twistringen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nordenham" title="Nordenham">Nordenham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oldenburg" title="Oldenburg">Oldenburg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Verden_an_der_Aller" title="Verden an der Aller">Verden an der Aller</a>. The network lies completely within the area of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Verkehrsverbund_Bremen/Niedersachsen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Verkehrsverbund Bremen/Niedersachsen (page does not exist)">Bremen-Lower Saxony Transport Association</a>, whose tariff structure applies.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bremen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>Every year since 1036, in the last two weeks of October, Bremen has hosted the <a href="/wiki/Freimarkt" title="Freimarkt">Freimarkt</a> ("Free market"), one of the world's oldest and in Germany one of today's biggest continuously celebrated fairground festivals.</li>
<li>Bremen is host to one of the four big annual <a href="/wiki/Techno" title="Techno">Techno</a> parades, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vision_Parade&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Vision Parade (page does not exist)">Vision Parade</a>.</li>
<li>Bremen is also host of the "Bremer 6 Tage Rennen" a bicycle race at the Bremen Arena.</li>
<li>Every year the city plays host to young musicians from across the world, playing in the International Youth Symphony Orchestra of Bremen (IYSOB).</li>
<li>On March 12, 1999, the rock band <a href="/wiki/Kiss_(band)" title="Kiss (band)">Kiss</a> played a live show in Bremen. Before the show, they were told by the fire marshall not to use any fireworks. They did not use any fireworks until the very end, when they set off all of the fireworks at once. Because of this, they are now banned from playing in Bremen.</li>
<li>Bremen was host to the 2006 RoboCup competition.</li>
<li>Bremen was host to the 32nd <a href="/wiki/Deutscher_Evangelischer_Kirchentag" class="mw-redirect" title="Deutscher Evangelischer Kirchentag">Deutscher Evangelischer Kirchentag</a>, 20–24 May 2009.</li>
<li>Bremen hosted the 50th <a href="/wiki/International_Mathematical_Olympiad" title="International Mathematical Olympiad">International Mathematical Olympiad</a> (IMO) from 10–22 July 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bremen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Weserstadion(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Weserstadion%282%29.jpg/220px-Weserstadion%282%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Weserstadion%282%29.jpg/330px-Weserstadion%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Weserstadion%282%29.jpg/440px-Weserstadion%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Weserstadion(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Weserstadion" class="mw-redirect" title="Weserstadion">Weserstadion</a> (<a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football (soccer)</a> stadium)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bremen is home to the <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team <a href="/wiki/SV_Werder_Bremen" title="SV Werder Bremen">SV Werder Bremen</a>, who won the <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_football_champions" title="List of German football champions">German Football Championship</a> for the fourth time and the German Football Cup for the fifth time in 2004, making them only the fourth team in German football history to win the double; the club won the German Football Cup for the sixth time in 2009. Only <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> has won more titles. In the final match of the 2009–10 season, Werder Bremen lost to Bayern Munich. The home stadium of SV Werder Bremen is the <a href="/wiki/Weserstadion" class="mw-redirect" title="Weserstadion">Weserstadion</a>, a pure football stadium, almost completely surrounded by solar cells. It is one of the biggest buildings in Europe delivering alternative energy.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_sciences">Education and sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bremen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Education and sciences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>With 18000 students,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bremen" title="University of Bremen">University of Bremen</a> is the largest university in Bremen, and is also home to the international <a href="/wiki/Goethe-Institut" title="Goethe-Institut">Goethe-Institut</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Fallturm_Bremen" title="Fallturm Bremen">Fallturm Bremen</a>. Additionally, Bremen has a <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Arts_Bremen" title="University of the Arts Bremen">University of the Arts</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bremen_University_of_Applied_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Bremen University of Applied Sciences">Bremen University of Applied Sciences</a>. In 2001, the private <a href="/wiki/Jacobs_University_Bremen" title="Jacobs University Bremen">Jacobs University Bremen</a> was founded. All major German research foundations maintain institutes in Bremen, with a focus set on marine sciences: The <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Society" title="Max Planck Society">Max Planck Society</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Marine_Microbiology" title="Max Planck Institute for Marine Microbiology">Max Planck Institute for Marine Microbiology</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_Wilhelm_Leibniz_Scientific_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="Gottfried Wilhelm Leibniz Scientific Community">Gottfried Wilhelm Leibniz Scientific Community</a> with the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.zmt-bremen.de/en/zmt.html">Center for Tropical Marine Ecology (zmt)</a>. The Bremerhaven-based <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Wegener_Institute_for_Polar_and_Marine_Research" title="Alfred Wegener Institute for Polar and Marine Research">Alfred-Wegener-Institute</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Helmholtz_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Helmholtz Association">Helmholtz Association</a> closely cooperates with the aforementioned institutes, especially within the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.marum.de/en/index.html">MARUM</a>, a center for marine environmental sciences, affiliated to the University of Bremen. Furthermore, The <a href="/wiki/Fraunhofer_Society" title="Fraunhofer Society">Fraunhofer Society</a> is present in Bremen with centers for applied material research <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ifam.fraunhofer.de/en.html">IFAM</a> and medical image computing <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.mevis.fraunhofer.de/">MEVIS</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Miscellanea">Miscellanea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bremen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Miscellanea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>In December 1949, Bremen hosted the lecture cycle <i>Einblick in das, was ist</i> by the philosopher <a href="/wiki/Martin_Heidegger" title="Martin Heidegger">Martin Heidegger</a>, in which Heidegger introduced his concept of a "fourfold" of earth and sky, gods and mortals. This was also Heidegger's first public-speaking engagement following his removal from his <a href="/wiki/Freiburg_im_Breisgau" title="Freiburg im Breisgau">Freiburg</a> professorship by the <a href="/wiki/Denazification" title="Denazification">Denazification</a> authorities.</li>
<li>Bremen is connected with a fairy tale by the <a href="/wiki/Brothers_Grimm" title="Brothers Grimm">Brothers Grimm</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Town_Musicians_of_Bremen" title="Town Musicians of Bremen">Town Musicians of Bremen</a></i>, although they never actually reach Bremen in the tale.</li>
<li>The 1922 film <i><a href="/wiki/Nosferatu" title="Nosferatu">Nosferatu</a>, eine Symphonie des Grauens</i> was set mostly in Bremen.</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_relations">Other relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bremen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Other relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>"Informal" relationships:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/India" title="India"><img alt="India" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/23px-Flag_of_India.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/35px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/45px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1350" data-file-height="900" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Pune" title="Pune">Pune</a>, India<sup id="cite_ref-BT_46-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom"><img alt="United Kingdom" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Dudley" title="Dudley">Dudley</a>, United Kingdom<sup id="cite_ref-BT_46-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia"><img alt="Namibia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_Namibia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Namibia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_Namibia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Namibia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_Namibia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Namibia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Windhoek" title="Windhoek">Windhoek</a>, Namibia<sup id="cite_ref-BT_46-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
